1.0 SUMMARY 

1.1 Introduction 

On March 26, 2009, B2Gold Corp. (B2Gold or the Company) completed the 100% acquisition of 

Central Sun Mining Inc. The primary assets acquired by B2Gold were the Limon Mine (95% 

interest) and the Libertad Mine (100% interest), both located in Nicaragua. Exploration by 

B2Gold in 2009 and 2010 culminated with the completion by B2Gold of an inferred resource in 

March 2011 of 3.545 million tonnes at an average grade of 4.58 grams per tonne (g/t) gold for 

522,393 contained ounces of gold on the Jabali vein target. The Jabali vein system as presently 

explored is considered a target of merit. The current average grade of ore being delivered to 

B2Gold's 5,500 tonne per day La Libertad mill is 1.6 g/t gold. This includes approximately 70% 

processed from open pit mining at a grade of 1.91 g/t gold and approximately 30% processed  

from spent ore from the historic leach pads, which has an average grade of 0.8 g/t gold. With 

the new Jabali resource grade of 4.58 g/t gold, B2Gold will have an opportunity to delay 

processing of the 30% spent ore until later in the mine life and replace it by processing 

potentially higher grade ore from the Jabali vein system. Additional drilling is required to 

upgrade the inferred resource to an indicated resource class prior to any decision being made 

on the economic viability of the Jabali vein system. It cannot be assumed that all or any part of 

an inferred mineral resource will ever be upgraded to a higher category. Inferred mineral 

resources are not mineral reserves and do not have demonstrated economic viability.  

This report was completed at the request of B2 Gold in order to comply with the standards set 

out in National Instrument 43-101 of the Canadian Securities Administrators. 

1.2 Location 

The Jabali vein is located within the La Libertad mineral concession which is located in the 

municipal area of La Libertad, Chontales Department, Republic of Nicaragua, approximately 

110 kilometres due east of Managua, the capital city of Nicaragua.  The geographic coordinates 

of the Jabali vein project are approximately 12° 13' N latitude, 85° 10' W longitude.  The datum 

survey point for the property group is pegged at 1,355,277.57 metres north and 704,476.63 

metres east, UTM Zone 16. The Jabali vein occurs just south of the town Santo Domingo. 

Access to the Jabali vein area is provided by a 10 kilometre secondary un-surfaced road that 

originates at the entrance to the town of La Libertad. 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 2  
   
 

1.3 History 

Underground mining operations in the Santo Domingo area first began in 1862 at the El Jabalí 

Mine and continued until the mid-1970s. The mine was developed on seven levels spaced 100 

feet apart. It is thought that the average grade mined was about 30 grams per tonne. No records 

of actual production have been located. 

1.4 Geology 

The Libertad mining district covers an area of approximately 150 square kilometres, and lies 

within a broad belt of Tertiary volcanic rocks that have been differentiated into two major units 

called the Matagalpa and the Coyol Groups. The Matagalpa Group is the oldest unit and 

consists of intermediate to felsic pyroclastic rocks that are unconformably overlain by Miocene-

aged mafic lavas of the Lower Coyol unit. The rocks of the Lower Coyol unit are the primary 

host lithology for the gold-bearing quartz veins in the Libertad district including the Jabali vein 

system. In the La Libertad district, these mineralized systems are classified as low-sulphidation 

epithermal quartz adularia veins. 

The Jabali vein structure occurs within a thick package of volcanic andesites. Epithermal quartz 

veins, quartz stockworks, quartz breccia and massive to banded quartz veins occur along the 

east-west trending mineralized structure. Alteration associated with the deposits is typical of a 

low sulphidation epithermal gold-silver deposit. Fracture-controlled quartz veining and 

silicification is surrounded by argillic and propylitic alteration zones within the andesite host rock. 

Quartz veins consist of milky white to light grey quartz with minor amounts of adularia. 

Epithermal textures comprise crustiform and colloform banding, vuggy and drusy quartz, 

cockscomb, and bladed silica pseudomorphs after low tempertature calcite.  Manganese oxides 

are common throughout the vuggy textured quartz, as linings and coatings on open spaces. 

Goethite, limonite, and jarosite are invariably present as coatings and linings to open spaces 

and fractures.  



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 3  
   
 

1.5 Exploration 

B2Gold completed 31 trenches along 3,200 metres of the Jabali vein structure in 2009 and 

2010. The encouraging results B2Gold obtained from trenching in 2009 led to the decision to 

drill 55 diamond drill holes (9,659.4 metres) on the Jabali vein in 2010.  

1.6 Sample Prep and Analysis 

Geotechnical logging was completed at the drill site to obtain the best geotechnical information 

prior to transporting the core to the logging facility at the La Libertad Mine site, 15 kilometres to 

the west. B2Gold maintained complete ownership of the logging, sampling, and transport of 

trench and drill samples so chain of custody of geologic data was in B2Gold's control until the 

samples reached the assay laboratory. 

Samples were pulverized at the La Libertad Mine lab using exploration dedicated crushing and 

pulverizing equipment by DESMINIC employees at the La Libertad Mine. Pulp samples were air 

freighted to Canada and fire assayed at the ALS Chemex Laboratory in North Vancouver. Each 

batch submitted to the primary lab contained certified standards as well as blanks and 

duplicates to monitor lab accuracy and precision. 

1.7 Data Verification 

Geologic data is dual entered and cross checked to detect transcription errors prior to being 

used for interpretation and modeling exercises. Assay data is received in digital format and 

verified through the use of duplicates, blanks and certified standards. Failed batch analysis are 

not permitted for use during resource estimation. Ten percent of all samples assayed at ALS 

Chemex were submitted to Skyline Laboratory in Tucson, Arizona for check analysis. No bias 

was noted and the assays compared within 5% and are suitable for use in resource estimation. 

In the Author's opinion, the database is reliable and valid for reporting inferred mineral 

resources. 

1.8 Modeling and Resource Estimation 

B2Gold built a geologic model of the Jabali vein on sections and levels based on logged 

geologic drill data. Three geological solid models were created within the mineralized structure; 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 4  
   
 

a quartz stock work model, and quartz breccia model and gallery model based on old stopes 

intercepted during the 2010 drill campaign. Three weathering models were also generated to 

account for colluvium, saprolite and saprock material. Raw assay were capped and gold and 

silver grades were estimated into a block model using ordinary kriging, inverse distance and 

nearest neighbor estimation techniques. Blocks were classified as inferred if they were 

estimated using two drill holes within a search ellipse of 90 x 25 x 65 metres (X,Y,Z) and at most 

75 metres to the nearest drill hole or two drill holes within a search ellipse of 120 x 37.5 x 97.5 

metres and at most 50 metres to the nearest drill hole. The procedures used in the construction 

of the geologic model and validation of the resource estimation meet or exceed industry 

accepted standards. Table 1-1 shows the Jabali undiluted insitu inferred resource reported 

above two cut off grades that was disclosed on March 31, 2011 by B2Gold.

vertically. Blocks below 50 metres and classified as Inferred are reported above a cut-off grade of 3.0 grams per tonne gold. 

2.  For the Central and Momotombo Zones, Inferred blocks are reported above a cut-off grade of 0.6 g/t gold between surface and 

100 metres vertically and above 3 g/t gold for inferred blocks below 100 metres. 

1.9 Recommendations 

The inferred resource estimate on the Jabali vein completed in 2011 indicates that the structure 

is a property of merit. An infill drill program is recommended to upgrade the inferred resource to 

an indicated resource classification. In addition, a series of close spaced drill holes (geostat 

cross) may be needed to evaluate short range grade variability along strike and down dip on the 

vein structure. Metallurgic testing should be initiated to evaluate the recovery characteristics of 

the gold bearing mineralization.  



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua

2.0 INTRODUCTION 

On March 31, 2011, B2Gold released the fourth quarter and December 31, 2010 resource and 

reserve statement. As this release contained disclosure of the first inferred mineral resource 

estimate on the Jabali vein system by B2Gold, B2Gold is required to prepare a technical report 

outlining the methodology of data collection, verification and procedures undertaken to complete 

the resource estimation in accordance with National Instrument 43-101. The inferred resource 

estimate was produced in house by B2Gold employees and reviewed by Qualified Persons 

employed by B2Gold. 

The March 31, 2011 news release also reported the total mineral reserves and resources on the 

La Libertad Property as of December 31, 2010 (see Table below).

4.0 RELIANCE ON OTHER EXPERTS 

This technical report is based on the Author's personal knowledge of La Libertad concession 

and Jabali vein system and a review of the published and un-published geologic data obtained 

from corporate and private sources by multiple authors. All sources of information are listed in 

the References section at the end of the technical report. Information pertinent to the report was 

collected by experienced geologists and technicians using acceptable industry procedures and 

protocols to provide a reliable database valid for resource estimation use.   

Information on the ownership status, mineral tenure positions and surface rights positions was 

provided by B2Gold's internal legal department. The Author has not reviewed any legal issues 

regarding land tenure nor independently verified the legal status or ownership of the property. 

The Author has relied on the expertise of B2Gold's internal legal counsel and Nicaraguan legal 

counsel, as to the status of the exploration concessions. 

5.0 PROPERTY DESCRIPTION AND LOCATION 

The Jabali vein is located within the La Libertad mineral tenement, which is located in the 

municipal area of La Libertad, Chontales Department, Republic of Nicaragua, approximately 

110 km due east of Managua, the capital city of Nicaragua.  The geographic coordinates of the 

project are approximately 12o 13' N latitude, 85o 10' W longitude.  The datum survey point for 

the property group is pegged at 1,355,277.57 m north and 704,476.63 m east, UTM Zone 16. A 

map showing the property location is presented in Figure 5-1.

Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua

Figure 5-1:  Location of the La Libertad Mine, Nicaragua 

To carry out exploration activities such as geophysics, geochemisty, trenching and drilling, 

permits are required in Nicaragua from the Ministry of Natural Resources and Environment 

(MARENA). Following the submission of a plan of work report and an Environmental Impact 

Study to MARENA, exploration work including diamond drilling, trenching, soil sampling and 

geological mapping was permitted under Administrative Resolution No. 08-2008, dated May 12, 

2008 and issued to DESMINIC by MARENA. B2Gold is operating under that Permit issued on 

May 12th, 2008 with new exploration programs added to the existing permit as addendums. 

Environmental baseline characterization studies for the area have not been completed since 

1995-1996. During that time monitoring was conducted for flora, fauna, hydrology, soils, air 

quality, and an economic baseline survey was completed. A Scope of Work for an updated 

baseline was approved by MARENA in 2008. Since that time, DESMINIC has been monitoring 

surface water quality samples and have identified high levels of suspended solids and 

occasional high levels (when compared to background values) of heavy metals in surface water 

samples due to farming, activities at a landfill located within the license area, and illegal

Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua

12 May 2011  Page 10  
   
 

artisanal mining on the concession. Additional baseline parameters that will be collected 

include: existing land disturbance, topography, geology, climate, air quality, surface and 

groundwater hydrology, surface and groundwater quality, flora, soils, seismicity, fauna, 

archaeology, protected areas, land use, and socioeconomics. 

Surface land rights in the Jabali area are presently owned by private parties and the mayorality 

of the town of Santo Domingo. The Company negotiated with the land owners to obtain surface 

access to conduct exploration carried out in the area in 2009 and 2010. The Company has 

purchased the surface rights over approximately 50% of the area of the current Jabali inferred 

mineral resource and is currently negotiating the purchase of the remainder. 

5.1 Mineral Tenure 

B2Gold is a publicly listed company that trades on the Toronto Stock Exchange (TSX) under the 

symbol BTO. 

B2Gold indirectly holds a 100% interest in Desarollo Minero de Nicaragua, S.A. (DESMINIC), a 

company incorporated under the laws of Nicaragua. DESMINIC is the Landlord with legitimate 

possession and ownership of all the land where mining concessions are granted at La Libertad; 

which together comprise La Libertad, Buenaventura and Cuernos de Oro concessions. 

DESMINIC, is a recognized Nicaraguan company (RUC No. 120500-9040) that was publicly 

authorized by Public Notary of Nicaragua, Dr. Alejandro Carrion Abaunza on May 12, 2000 and 

Inscribed with # 962, pages 357/381, volume 32, Book Two of Corporations; and inscribed with 

No. 5170, page 273/274, volume 12 of the Book of Persons, both of the Public Registry of 

Masaya. 

The La Libertad mining concession was granted in August 31, 1994 for the term of 40 years 

pursuant to Ministerial Decree No. 032-RN-MC/94.  This concession was granted and is 

regulated under the old, pre-2001 mining law.  The location of the concession, called the La 

Libertad Exploitation Concession, is shown in Figure 5-2.  The principal obligations under the 

Ministerial Accord include the payment annually of surface taxes, and a net 3.0 percent royalty 

on gross production revenues.  



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 11  
   
 

Another royalty interest was granted to a corporation formed by La Libertad workers (IMISA). 

The Royalty Contract dated September 25, 1996 (Public Deed No. 23) grants a royalty on Net 

Smelter Returns equal to 2.0 percent of the total production of gold and silver from La Libertad 

Exploitation Concession to IMISA. 

The total royalty payable on La Libertad Mine production is 5.0 percent.  

In addition to La Libertad Exploitation Concession, DESMINIC has two exploration concessions. 

The first is called La Buena Ventura I (2,350 ha), granted under the new mining code enacted in 

2001. The Buena Ventura I concession was granted in July 2002 for a period of 25 years 

pursuant to Ministerial Decree No. 200-RN-MC/2002.  The second is called Cuernos de Oro 

(1,196 ha), granted under the new mining code enacted in 2001. The Cuernos de Oro 

concession was granted in June 2008 for a period of 25 years pursuant to Ministerial Decree 

No. 18-DM-101-2008. 

B2Gold also owns 80% of the Cerro Quiroz claim that lies contiguous to and east of the La 

Libertad concession. This was obtained in 2010 from Condor Resources PLC (Condor), a 

company listed on the Alternative Investment Market of the London Stock Exchange, via a claim 

swap. Condor and B2Gold have agreed to incorporate two new companies in Nicaragua, La 

India Gold SA and Cerro Quiroz Gold S.A. and transfer the Cerro Quiroz, Espinito-San Pablo 

and La India concessions to the new companies. The principal terms of the transaction are: 

1. La India Gold SA will be 80% directly owned by Condor and 20% indirectly by 

B2Gold. 

2. Cerro Quiroz Gold SA will be 80% indirectly owned by B2Gold and 20% directly by 

Condor. 

3. B2Gold will cause the transfer of La India and Espinito-San Pablo concessions (both 

in La India District) to La India Gold SA and Condor the transfer of Cerro Quiroz 

Concession to Cerro Quiroz Gold SA. The transfer of the concessions was approved 

by the Ministry of Energy and Mines. 

4. The 80% shareholder of each new company shall complete at their own cost, not 

less than 2,000 metres of drilling on the concession under their 80% ownership 

within 2 years of receiving all permits required to drill including land access rights.

6.0 ACCESSIBILITY, CLIMATE, LOCAL RESOURCES, INFRASTRUCTURE AND 
PHYSIOGRAPHY 

Access to the La Libertad Concession from Managua is via a well maintained paved highway to 

Juigalpa (201 km), and subsequently via a good, hand paved road (30 km) traveling eastward to 

the village of La Libertad. This route entails three hours of travel in a four-wheel drive vehicle. 

From the village of La Libertad, the Jabali vein area is accessible year round by gravel road 

between the towns of La Libertad and Santo Domingo, approximately 10 km east of the town of 

La Libertad. 

6.1 Climate 

The La Libertad property is situated in the central highlands of Nicaragua with a climate defined 

by a pronounced wet and dry season. The wet season occurs in May through to November, with 

the highest precipitation occurring usually in September and October.  Average monthly rainfall 

during these months is approximately 270 mm. The driest months are generally in February and 

March, with average monthly rainfalls of approximately 23 mm. According to government 

statistical records, the Department of Chontales has an average annual rainfall of 1,695 mm. At 

the La Libertad weather station, the average annual precipitation recorded over a 16-year period 

(1972 to 1987) was 1,687 mm. 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 14  
   
 

Temperature variation in Nicaragua is mainly a function of altitude. Nationally, temperature 

varies between 21°C in the upper parts of the central mountain ranges to 29°C in the Pacific 

coastal regions. Average temperatures recorded in Chontales region range from 24°C in 

December to 27°C in May. The average daily temperature is fairly constant at 25°C during the 

rest of the year. 

6.2 Local Resources 

Most of the staff at the La Libertad Mine originate from the surrounding towns in the area. The 

town of La Libertad has a municipal and rural population of approximately 11,400 persons, while 

the town of Santo Domingo located just north of the Jabali vein structure has a municipal and 

rural population of 12,200 people. The area has a long history of mining and ranching, and a 

local labour forced skilled in small-scale mining is available. Some of the higher-skilled jobs, 

such as supervisory and professional designations, are filled by expatriates. Most machinery 

and equipment required at the mine is imported.   

6.3 Infrastructure 

Mining and processing of ore commenced at the Libertad Mine in the fourth quarter of 2009 

following the completion of the conversion of the Libertad Mine from a heap leach mine to a 

conventional milling operation. The Libertad mill was originally designed to process 3,500 

tonnes of ore per day (tpd). A second ball mill was installed and commissioned in 2010, which 

increased the design throughput to approximately 5,500 tonnes per day. The mine and process 

facilities normally operate year round, with short delays during the worst of the wet season. 

Road access to the mine provides for overland movement of all required supplies and materials.  

Open pit mining of both ore and waste has been undertaken by an independent mining 

contractor using the contractor's equipment fleet. Drilling and blasting for mining will be added to 

the contractor's scope of work for future operations. The mine operation maintains a local road 

system to service the operations needs. The majority of the mine workers reside locally and are 

transported to the mine site on a daily basis.   

Accommodation, food and material supplies are all available locally. High-tension power lines 

provide power to the town of Santo Domingo, although power supply can be limited at times. 

Cell phone coverage in the area is very good allowing communication with major centers in 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 15  
   
 

country and internationally. Local rivers are able to supply adequate water for large scale mining 

operations throughout the year. 

6.4 Physiography 

The area is characterized by hilly terrain ranging in elevation from 400 metres to 835 metres 

above sea level. Many of the old workings in the region are located on hills and ridges. Gold 

mineralization is associated with quartz veins that support these topographic highs. Cerro El 

Chamarro, located five kilometres northeast of the town of La Libertad, is the highest point on 

the concession at 835.2 metres above sea level. 

The La Libertad Mine is situated in the western end of the exploitation concession, 

approximately four kilometres northwest of the town of La Libertad. Prior to open pit mining, a 

mineralized vein outcropped along the Cerro Mojón ridge. It was the highest point in the 

immediate area at approximately 630 metres above sea level but has since been removed by 

mining. The surrounding topography is characterized by gently sloping terrain, reaching a low of 

approximately 500 metres above sea level. Vegetative cover is primarily second growth shrubs, 

small trees, and grasses. 

The Jabali vein is situated on an east-west topographic ridge just south of the town of Santo 

Domingo, located 10 kilometres east of the town of La Libertad.  

7.0 HISTORY 

During the past century, mining and ranching have been the main economic activities in the 

area, with mines in the La Libertad-Santo Domingo area developed by large companies, small 

local ventures, and individual miners. Individually, the local miners and prospectors are known 

as güiriseros, or small miners. In the past, both large and small mine operations typically 

employed stamp mills and arrastras (small primitive mills) for processing ore, and mercury 

amalgamation techniques to recover the gold. In the mid-1950s, larger scale mining companies 

began to use more conventional milling, gravity separation techniques and cyanide to recover 

the gold in local deposits. 

Underground mining operations in the Santo Domingo area first began in 1862 at the El Jabalí 

Mine and continued until the mid 1970s. Important mines developed during this period include: 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 16  
   
 

El Jabalí, which belonged to Companía Anónima de El Jabalí; Monte Carmelo, owned by 

Victoria Salinas; and La Tranca, owned by the Pellas and Company. No larger-scale mining 

operations have been in production in the Santo Domingo area for the last 20 years; however, 

small miner activity and "arrastra" (local artisanal milling) operations have continued. 

Larger scale mining operations at La Libertad started in the middle of the last century at the San 

Juan and Babilonia areas. From 1900 to 1935, British companies extracted mineralized rock 

from the Santa Elena, Crimea, Santa María, San Juan, Tres Amigos, Zopilote, and Azul areas. 

Approximately 200,000 tonnes of ore, with an average grade of 15 g/t gold, was mined during 

this time. The ore was processed at a rate of 20 tpd to 40 tpd using a stamp mill. Gold was 

recovered by mercury amalgamation techniques. 

From 1943 to 1945, the Neptune Mining Company conducted geological exploration in the 

Santa Elena and Santa María areas, however, no mining took place. From 1956 to 1979, an 

American company, Lemans Resource, mined the Santa Elena-Crimea deposit. The ore was 

processed in a mill at a rate of 40 stpd.  Gold was recovered through flotation and cyanidation of 

the concentrate. 

Prior to the Sandinista period, Nicaragua was an important contributor in the Central American 

gold market. In November 1979, the Sandinista government nullified all mining concessions 

issued by the previous administration and nationalized all mining companies operating in the 

country. As a result, average annual gold production for the period 1975 through 1979 dropped 

to an estimated 69,400 troy ounces. 

Throughout the 1980s, the Sandinista government sought assistance for the mining sector in 

both Western and Eastern Europe. The United Kingdom, the Soviet Union, Sweden, and 

Bulgaria all provided institutional support to the Nicaraguan mining industry. However, due to 

low availability of capital most facilities had to make do with old and substandard equipment. 

Large-scale mining operations at La Libertad were suspended in November 1979 until the 

mining industry was nationalized in 1981. In 1982, mining of the Santa Elena deposit resumed 

under INMINE (Instituto Nicaragüense de la Minería). From 1984 to 1989, a crushing and 

grinding facility was installed and the capacity of the mill increased from 40 stpd to 120 stpd, 

using the same flotation/cyanidation technology for gold recovery. Tailings were being dumped 

directly into the Río El Tigre until a tailings dam was constructed northeast of the mill in 1988.  



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 17  
   
 

Mining operations at Santa Elena were suspended in 1991 and the San Juan vein became the 

main source of ore. 

In 1991, the Chamorro Administration began its efforts to privatize Nicaraguan mining 

enterprises as part of an overall plan for economic stabilization and structural reform. It was 

hoped that foreign investment would boost mining production and provide employment and 

stability in regions dependent on mining. The Chamorro Administration agreed to privatize 25 

percent of the national mineral resources to the Nicaraguan mine workers. This resulted in the 

formation of Inversiones Mineras S.A. (IMISA), a profit-oriented company privately held by the 

Nicaraguan mine workers. Technical and administrative assistance for IMISA was contracted 

from former INMINE officials. The remaining interest in select facilities was put out to 

international tender. 

La Libertad went out to tender in 1992. On April 11, 1994, a Presidential Decree was issued 

authorizing the privatization of La Libertad mining assets. Effective August 26, 1994, an 

agreement between Greenstone de Nicaragua S.A. (GRENICA), a wholly owned subsidiary of 

Greenstone Resources Canada Ltd., and IMISA resulted in the formation of a new company 

called Minera Nicaragüence S.A. (MINISA). The new company was formed with the purpose of 

developing a large-scale gold mining operation out of the small La Libertad operation. At this 

time, small miners were active on site, processing their gold using arrastras and mercury 

amalgamation. 

MINISA was originally owned 75% (51,450 shares) by GRENICA and 25% (17,150 shares) by 

IMISA (68,600 total shares). IMISA vested in its 25% of MINISA by virtue of contributing the 

existing assets at La Libertad, including the exploitation and exploration concessions (which 

included a 3% royalty payable to the Nicaraguan government). These assets were conveyed to 

IMISA by the Nicaraguan government and the IMISA shares were pledged to the Nicaraguan 

government, until such time as IMISA paid $1,715,000 to the government. GRENICA became 

vested once it had contributed a total of $5.325 million to the project and issued 468,100 

Greenstone Common Shares. 

As a requirement of privatization, MINISA was required to complete a feasibility study for an 

operation producing greater than 50,000 ounces of gold per year. Compliance was met with the 

submittal of a feasibility study in October 1995.  GRENICA was required to fund the feasibility as 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 18  
   
 

well as any cash losses from the existing operation. It was also required to fund a limited 

rehabilitation program of the existing operation. At December 31, 1995, GRENICA had met all 

vesting conditions for the 75% interest in MINISA. 

In September 1996, GRENICA acquired the remaining 25% minority interest from IMISA 

through the acquisition of all the shares of MINISA held by IMISA. The purchase price consisted 

of:  

• a cash payment of $13,125,000, directed by IMISA to be paid to shareholders;  

• a cash payment of approximately $350,000 in satisfaction of existing obligations to 

IMISA in connection with GRENICA's and IMISA's shareholdings in MINISA; and  

• a 2% net smelter royalty in favour of IMISA on future production from areas within 

the La Libertad mining area.  

Under MINISA, La Libertad mine site was rehabilitated and operations continued from mid-1994 

until October 1996, when MINISA shut down the operation to prepare for the heap leach 

operation. 

GRENICA, through MINISA, operated the mine from 1997 to mid-1999, mining 3.1 million 

tonnes at a grade of 1.9 g/t gold and producing 103,000 ounces of gold. 

By 1999, GRENICA was suffering financial difficulties, and all mining and exploration activities 

at La Libertad ceased in August of that year. Leslie Coe, an individual investor acquired MINISA 

by repaying GRENICA's debt to vendors. The name of the new company was Desarollo Minero 

de Nicaragua S.A. (DESMINIC). In February 2001, Leslie Coe sold 50% of DESMINIC to RNC 

Resources Limited (RNC), a private international business incorporated in Belize in March 2001, 

and 40% to Auric Resources Corp. Leslie Coe retained a 10% interest in DESMINIC. 

In early 2001, DESMINIC rehabilitated the heap leach operation at La Libertad, and resumed 

operations.  

In July 2003, RNC acquired Auric Resources Corp.'s interest in DESMINIC and, in September 

2003, Leslie Coe's remaining 10% interest, thereby obtaining 100% ownership. RNC Gold Inc., 

a publicly traded Canadian company, became the owner of all the assets of RNC, including 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 19  
   
 

DESMINIC, in December 2003 as a result of a reverse take-over of Tango Mineral Resources 

Inc. by RNC and a name change of Tango Mineral Resources Inc. to RNC Gold Inc.  

In February 2006, Yamana Gold Inc. acquired DESMINIC along with all the other assets of RNC 

Gold Inc. as a result of a merger between the two companies.  

Operations from 2001 to 2007 were mostly continuous, with some temporary shutdowns 

reported as being for maintenance purposes. Mine production has been largely from a series of 

pits along the main Mojón-Crimea structure. Significant production was also achieved from the 

Esmeralda structure located parallel to and immediately south of the Mojón pits. Mine 

production for 2001 to March, 2007 totaled 6.7 million tonnes, at a grade of 1.66 g/t gold, 

producing 207,000 ounces of gold. 

On July 6, 2006, Glencairn Gold Corporation (Glencairn) purchased a 100% interest in La 

Libertad from Yamana Gold Inc., along with a 60% interest in the Cerro Quema Gold Project in 

Panama. The total consideration for the above two acquisitions was 32 million Glencairn 

common shares. 

AMEC conducted testwork and studied potential for conversion of the heap leach process to 

conventional milling for Glencairn, completing a scoping study in May 2007. Results were 

positive, and open pit mining was halted in March 2007 in order to proceed with the process 

upgrade. Glencairn commissioned a feasibility study, and investigated sources of mill 

equipment. 

Glencairn underwent a name change to Central Sun Mining Inc. (Central Sun) on November 29, 

2007. Along with the corporate name change, the La Libertad operation was renamed the Orosi 

Mine. 

On March 26, 2009, B2Gold acquired 100% of the shares of Central Sun by way of a plan of 

arrangement. At that time, the Libertad mine was under redevelopment from a heap leach to a 

milling operation and B2Gold continued that process and finalized construction during 2009. 

Ore processing at La Libertad Mine recommenced on December 15, 2009 with the first doré bar 

produced on January 5, 2010. B2Gold projects the La Libertad Mine to produce approximately 

80,000 to 90,000 ounces of gold annually over an initial seven year mine life. The La Libertad 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua

12 May 2011  Page 20  
   
 

mill was originally designed to process 3,500 tonnes of ore per day. A second ball mill, which 

was not included in the original plant design, was installed and commissioned at La Libertad 

Mine in 2010. 

8.0 GEOLOGICAL SETTING 

8.1 Regional Geology 

Nicaragua is divided into five provinces that reflect the country's geological make-up: the 

Coastal Plains of the Pacific, the Nicaraguan Depression or Graben, the Central Interior 

Province, the Northern Province and the Plains of the Atlantic Coast. 

The Jabali deposit is located in the Libertad gold district which covers an area of approximately 

150 km2 within the Central Province. The deposit lies within a broad belt of Tertiary volcanic 

rocks that have been differentiated into two major units called the Matagalpa and the Coyol 

Groups (McBirney and Williams, 1965; Pearsons, 1972). The Oligocene to Miocene age 

Matagalpa Group consists of intermediate to felsic pyroclastic rocks. Unconformably overlying 

the Matagalpa Group are Miocene-aged mafic to intermediate lavas of the Lower Coyol unit. 

The rocks of the Lower Coyol unit host the gold-bearing quartz veins in the Libertad gold district. 

Pliocene-age mafic lavas and ignimbrites, belonging to the 400 m to 600 m thick Upper Coyol 

unit, form mesa-like erosional remnants in the region (Darce, 1990). Several small felsic to 

mafic intrusive bodies of similar Tertiary age are distributed along northeast-southwest structural 

trends. 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 21  
   
 

 

Figure 8-1:  Regional Geology, Libertad Property, Chontales Department, Nicaragua 

8.2 Property Geology 

The Jabali low sulphidation epithermal quartz adularia vein system is hosted in a thick sequence 

of andesitic flows believed to be part of the Lower Coyol Group. The group consists of 

individual, feldspar porphyritic andesitic flows ranging in thickness from two metres to five 

metres to much larger flows 22 metres to 50 metres in thickness. Lapilli-tuff and occasionally 

ash tuff beds of variable thickness separate the flows. 

The east-west trending Jabali vein system has been traced on surface over a distance of more 

than six kilometres. To date, ongoing diamond drilling has tested more than 3,950 metres of the 

Jabali vein system. The vein system dips to the north, varying from 60o to 80o north. 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 22  
   
 

The andesite flows host the epithermal quartz veins, quartz stockworks, quartz breccia and 

massive to banded quartz veins along the east-west trending mineralized structure. 

Alteration associated with the deposits is typical of a low sulphidation epithermal quartz adularia 

vein system. Fracture-controlled quartz veining and silicification is surrounded by argillic and 

propylitic alteration zones within the andesite host rock. 

Quartz veins consist of milky white to light grey quartz with minor amounts of adularia. 

Epithermal textures comprise crustiform and colloform banding, vuggy and drusy quartz, 

cockscomb, and bladed silica pseudomorphs after low tempertature calcite.   

Manganese oxides are ubiquitous and observed to be very strong throughout the vuggy 

textured quartz, as linings and coatings on open spaces. Goethite, limonite, and jarosite are 

invariably present as coatings and linings to open spaces and fractures.  

Silicification is often intense within the vein zones. Partial silica replacement and rimming of 

breccia clasts is widespread throughout the veins and can extend into both the hanging wall and 

footwall.  

 

Figure 8-2:  La Libertad area geology 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 23  
   
 

9.0 DEPOSIT TYPE 

The Jabali vein system is a low-sulphidation epithermal quartz adularia vein system with the 

following geologic characteristics that support the model: 

• Back arc tectonic setting 

• Lack of an associated intrusive source 

• Banded fissure veins – structural control 

• Crustiform and colloform banding, vuggy and drusy quartz, cockscomb texture and 

bladed silica pseudomorphs after low temperature calcite 

• Adularia noted within the veins and breccias 

10.0 MINERALIZATION 

The Jabali vein system as presently known is geologically similar to other known veins within 

the La Libertad Concession. Gold mineralization on the La Libertad concession occurs within an 

epithermal vein field that is 2.5 kilometers wide and extends along strike for at least 20 

kilometres. Individual veins (excluding Jabali) vary in strike length from 200-300 metres and up 

to 3000 metres (Mojon-Crimea) trend. Fluid inclusion work from vein samples further west from 

Jabali indicates fluid temperatures varying between 172° to 316°C during mineralization. 

(Alvarez, 2008). Quartz vein textures observed in drill core at Jabali as well as other veins on 

the concession are consistent with variable fluid temperatures. Multiple brecciation events as 

well as colloform banded and replacement textures are common at Jabali as well as other vein 

systems like Mojon, Crimea and Santa Maria within the La Libertad concession.   

Gold mineralization at Jabali is hosted in the east-west, northerly dipping quartz vein, quartz 

breccia and quartz stockwork system. The 6.2 kilometre long vein system has been divided into 

two zones: Jabali Antenna to the west of the Rio Soucio and Jabali Central to the east. 

Preliminary multi-element geochemical data in conjunction with drill core logging suggests gold 

values are associated with the presence of gold-silver sulphosalt mineralization and locally with 

zinc and possibly lead sulphides.  The vein structure is commonly oxidized up to 60 metres 

below surface. Gold values within this oxidized portion of the vein are commonly associated with 

increased limonite, jarosite and manganese oxides within vuggy textured quartz breccia veins. 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 24  
   
 

Sulphides are rare near surface due to moderate to strong oxidation within the structure. Jabali 

Antenna has been drill tested over a strike length of 1,300 metres. The vein system in the 

current resource ranges in width from 5 to 29 metres, dips 60o to 70o to the north and has 

vertical extent that ranges from 150 to 250 metres.  

Jabali Central has been drill tested over a strike length of 2,650 metres. The vein system in the 

current resource ranges in width from 5 to 13 metres, dips 80o to the north and has a vertical 

extent of 50 to 150 metres as presently drilled. 

Previous work by others within the La Libertad district have shown that anomalous gold is 

associated with increased levels of potassic and silica alteration as well sulphides which are 

often oxidized to limonite and hematite (Hodder, 2008). These studies and conclusions were not 

based on work done on the Jabali vein structure however field observations by B2Gold in 2010 

are in general agreement. 

11.0 EXPLORATION 

11.1 Introduction (B2Gold 2009 – to present) 

In 2009, B2Gold began a mapping and sampling program of the La Libertad concession on a 

number of low sulphidation epithermal veins along the 20 kilometre epithermal gold vein district. 

This initial exploration included a review of the six kilometre long Jabali structure (partially mined 

historically for high grade gold material). The objective was to identify several vein systems that 

exhibited potential for low grade, open pit potential. Initial mapping and trenching of the Jabali 

system identified mineralization up to 50 metres wide  as well as narrow, high grade 

mineralization up to 194.6 grams per tonne gold over 1.3 metres. B2Gold completed 17 

trenches for 537 metres in 2009 on the Jabali vein system. Favourable gold assay results from 

trenching in 2009 resulted in the decision by B2Gold to drill the Jabali vein structure in 2010. 

12.0 EXPLORATION DRILLING BY B2GOLD ON THE LA LIBERTAD CONCESSION 

B2Gold commenced drilling on the Libertad mine property on February 19, 2010. Total drilling 

completed in 2010 amounted to 130 drill holes for 20,095 metres. During 2010, B2Gold 

continued to explore the La Libertad gold belt and focused on infill drilling of inferred resources 

on known vein systems on the property. Drilling began on the Jabali vein system in February 

2010 and focused on the Antenna and Central Zones, two zones that have a combined strike 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 25  
   
 

length of 3,200 metres of the known 6.2 kilometre strike length. The objective of B2Gold's 2010 

drill program was to initiate drilling of the promising Jabali vein system, infill drill the eastern 

portion of the San Juan vein structure and expand the western margins of the Mojon and 

Crimea pits. In addition several other regional vein targets were drill tested.

The Jabali vein system dips steeply 60-80 degrees north, as a result the majority (88%) of the 

2010 drill holes were drilled with an azimuth of 180 degrees. Down-hole surveys were collected 

every 50 metres down hole by the drill contractor using a Reflex Maxibor II optical borehole 

survey system. Drill hole collar locations were located using a total station GPS unit. Two 

surveys were performed; the first to locate the proposed hole position and the second one after 

the hole was completed to get a final hole survey location. All aspects of Jabali vein drill 

program, including collar surveying, down-hole surveying, geologic data collection, sampling, 

and quality control were supervised by Mr. Vern Shein, B2Gold Exploration Manager for La 

Libertad Mine. 

13.0 SAMPLING METHOD AND APPROACH 

13.1 General Remarks 

B2Gold has developed sampling protocols and manuals that outline procedures for the 

collection of stream, soil, rock and drill core. These procedures are routinely updated and 

improved upon as required by the various project managers during the exploration programs. 

The sampling methods and procedures meet or exceed industry standards and the data 

collected and verified is considered valid for use in the mineral resource estimate. 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 27  
   
 

13.2 Core Handling & Logging 

Drill core recovery was measured at the drill site to record more accurate recovery 

characteristics prior to core transport to the logging facilities. The drill core was then secured in 

wooden boxes and transported from the drill site to the core logging facility at the La Libertad 

Mine facility by B2Gold personnel. The core box numbers and drill core recoveries were double 

checked at the core shack by the supervising geologist. Rock quality designation (RQD) 

measurements are recorded by a geologic technician under the supervision of the drill geologist. 

The geologic technician also recorded the number of geologic fractures, condition of joints, rock 

hardness according to the geotechnical logging manual from Vector Peru. 

Geologic data including rock type, weathering and oxidation, alteration, mineralization and 

structural features is collected on handwritten paper logs and subsequently double-entered into 

an excel spreadsheet and compared prior to importing the drill data into a database. 

Core Sampling: 

Drill core sample lengths were defined by the rig geologist based on geologic differences. 

Sampling breaks were based on variable percentages of quartz content, quartz types, amount 

of sulphides, alteration intensities and lithology contacts. Samples were collected continuously 

through mineralized zones as well as into the footwall and hanging wall host rocks. The average 

sampled core length was 0.65 metres. A breakdown of sample lengths is noted below in Table 

13-1. 

Drill core samples were cut in half using a diamond saw and placed in plastic bags with three 

sample tags to identify the reject, pulp and split pulp portion of the sample at the laboratory.   

Table 13-1:  Sample Lengths from 2010 Jabali Drill Campaign 

Range of Sample Lengths (m) # of Samples Percent

<0.5  730 16.0

0.5 to 0.99 3,451 80.0

Drill Core Photography: 

Each drill hole was completely photographed with a digital camera prior to sampling. Two boxes 

were photographed at one time in both a dry state and a wet state. The boxes are accompanied 

by a narrow white board identifying the drill hole number, box numbers and down hole depths.   

Geotechnical Logging: 

Geologic technicians record core recovery, core loss and percent recovery. Rock quality 

designation (RQD) is measured with care taken to discern between geologic fractures and drill-

induced fractures. The geologic technicians also record the number of fractures, condition of 

joints, rock and soil hardness according to the geotechnical logging manual from Vector Peru. 

This data is captured on paper and later entered into a digital database. 

Specific Gravity Measurements: 

The 2010 drill program on the Jabali vein system collected 564 samples for specific gravity 

measurements using a wax-coated water immersion method (see Appendix 3). Samples were 

dried five hours prior to measurement.  Fifteen to twenty centimetres lengths of core were tested 

periodically down hole at lithology and alteration changes and within the mineralized stockwork 

and vein mineralization. Samples were weighed with a digital balance that was routinely 

calibrated with brass calibration weights. QA/QC was maintained with a certified standard soda 

ash glass cylinder with a pre-determined density. The glass standard was inserted into the 

sample stream at least once every two batches of specific gravity samples that were tested.

13.3 Observations and Conclusions  

Based on the description of the sampling method provided by B2Gold, the sampling methods 

meet or exceed industry standard practices and are representative of the mineralization within 

the Jabali vein system. The QA/QC and data verification procedures implemented by B2Gold 

indicate that the data is valid for mineral resource estimations. 

Additional specific gravity samples should be collected in the saprolite (oxide) and saprock 

(transition) portion of the deposit during the next phase of drilling even though the oxide portion 

of the Jabali vein mineralization represents a small percentage of the deposit.  

14.0 SAMPLE PREPARATION, ANALYSES AND SECURITY 

14.1 General Remarks 

All samples collected on the Jabali vein including soil samples, rock samples and drill core 

samples were transported to La Libertad Mine laboratory for sample preparation and then air 

freighted to North Vancouver, British Columbia, Canada for gold analysis at ALS Chemex 

Laboratory, an ISO 9001:2000 certified international provider of analytical services to mining 

and exploration companies.  

Check assays were performed every three months using Skyline Labs in Tucson, Arizona. Ten 

percent of the Jabali database is selected for outside lab check analysis with samples selected 

that represent the total grade distribution but emphasize those samples with grades close to the 

cut-off grade of La Libertad Mine. 

Periodically, samples were assayed at the La Libertad Mine lab when quick results were needed 

to help guide exploration. These results are stored within the database but not used for the 

grade estimation exercise. 

14.2 Sample Preparation 

The Jabali vein inferred resource estimate is based on 9,659 metres of drilling and 4,563 

samples that were collected and assayed. B2Gold also inserted 596 quality control samples into 

the sample stream to monitor lab accuracy and precision representing 11.6% of the Jabali 

assay database.   



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 30  
   
 

Samples were transported from the drill site to the La Libertad Mine laboratory where they were 

crushed and pulverized by DESMINIC mine employees at the La Libertad Mine prior to shipping 

to ALS Chemex in North America. The samples were dried at 105º C to remove excess 

moisture (10 hours for core samples and 24 hours for rock samples). The entire dried core 

samples were crushed using a TM Terminator Crushing system to 75% to 85% passing 10 

mesh (2mm) specifications.  

An 800 gram split of the 10 mesh crusher material was pulverized using LM-2 pulverizers.  The 

800 gram samples were pulverized to produce a product that had 90% of the sample passing 

200-mesh screen (0.074 mm) specifications. Samples weighing 120 grams were split of the 800 

gram pulverized sample and placed into sealed plastic bags, which in turn were put inside small 

paper bags, each one marked with the sample number using a permanent marker. The top of 

the paper bags was folded and stapled. The sample batch including certified standards, blanks 

and duplicates were packed inside a cardboard box sealed with transparent tape and market on 

the outside with the sample sequence. Those boxes were sent to ALS Chemex in North 

Vancouver, Canada for gold and silver analysis.  

An additional 120 gram duplicate pulp were collected during the initial splitting of the pulverized 

samples and stored in sealed boxes by drill hole number. These extra pulps are periodically 

sent to a second outside laboratory as a check analysis or referee sample. 

B2Gold upgraded the exploration preparation facility at the mine lab with TM Terminator 

crushing systems and LM-2 pulverizers in 2010. A series of screen analysis are done daily on 

the crusher and pulverized products to ensure proper size fractions are being produced. It is the 

Author's opinion that the sample chain of custody, preparation procedures and sample security 

meet industry standards. 

14.3 Sample Analyses 

The 2010 drill core samples were analyzed for gold using ALS Chemex code Au-AA25 up until 

July 2010 and ALS code Au-AA26 for the remainder of 2010. Both are fire assay and atomic 

absorption procedures using 50 gram sample weights (AA25) and 30 gram sample weights 

(AA26). These procedures have a lower detection limit of 5 ppb and an upper limit of 10,000 

ppb. 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 31  
   
 

In cases where the analytical result exceeded 3,000 ppb gold, an additional 50 gram sample 

charge was re-run with a fire assay fusion and gravimetric procedure (ALS Chemex procedure 

Au-GRA-21) which has a lower limit of 0.05 ppm and an upper limit of 1,000 ppm.  

Eleven drill holes from the 2010 drill campaign were also selected to be analyzed for 37 

elements using inductively coupled plasma and atomic emission spectroscopy (ICP-AES), using 

protocol ME-ICP-61 at the ALS Chemex's lab in North Vancouver, Canada.  

14.4 Sample Security 

Once drill holes were logged and sampled, drill core samples with sample number tags were 

sealed within plastic bags by tamper proof "zap-straps" or cords.  Sample numbers were also 

recorded on the outside of the bags. The samples were transported by truck to the La Libertad 

Mine laboratory by company vehicles and personnel. All sampling of B2Gold core was 

conducted within La Libertad Mine compound and by exploration personnel under the 

supervision of the drill geologists. Sample batches of 78 samples with sequential sample 

numbers were submitted to the lab to ensure that B2Gold knew where the quality control 

samples were within any fusion run within the lab batch analysis. Coarse rejects are stored in a 

locked warehouse at La Libertad Mine in well labeled bags. 

Boxed sample batches were transported to Managua by B2Gold personnel in company 

vehicles. Samples were stored in a locked compound in Managua prior to air shipment to 

Canada. 

14.5 Observations and Conclusions 

B2Gold's procedures and protocols for sample collection, chain of custody, sampling and 

analysis have been developed and optimized by the management and Qualified Persons within 

the Company for 20 years. The practices are consistently monitored and verified by site 

database managers, country database managers and ultimately by the Author as well as a 

Vancouver-based Company wide database manager. Monthly reports are submitted by the 

project managers as well as a separate quality control monthly report that track both the 

preparation laboratory performance as well as the primary and referee lab performance. It is the 

Author's opinion that sample preparation, analysis and QAQC monitoring meet or exceed 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 32  
   
 

industry standards and the sample results are adequate for use in estimating an inferred mineral 

resource. 

15.0 DATA VERIFICATION 

15.1 Assaying Quality Assurance and Quality Control (QA/QC) Program 

Industry-standard quality control programs have been employed for the 2010 and ongoing 2011 

drilling campaigns at La Libertad. 

B2Gold caters their individual batch sizes and QA/QC insertion frequency to the oven size used 

by the primary laboratory, ALS Minerals in Vancouver.  An oven batch consists of 78 samples.  

Each half batch of 39 samples includes a standard, a blank, a field duplicate, a preparation 

duplicate, and a pulp duplicate.  Certified reference materials (standards) were sourced from 

CDN Labs in Vancouver, BC, Canada.  A coarse field blank material composed of basalt is 

sourced from a quarry located in Nindiri, Nicaragua. 

Approximately 10% of all samples were submitted for check assay by a secondary laboratory, in 

this case, Skyline Assayers & Laboratories of Tucson Arizona. The check assay data was 

compared with the original analyses. The overall grade difference between the labs is less than 

5%. 

Sample Type # of Samples Percentage 

Original 4,563 88

B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 33  
   
 

All assay data was received in digital format from the lab and imported directly into a project 

specific database for validation. Evaluation of the performance of QA/QC insertions was done 

immediately upon receipt/import of the laboratory assay certificate. The database contains tools 

designed to facilitate the validation of results and the presentation of QA/QC data. 

A lab submittal batch failed if a certified standard assay was +/- 3 standard deviations from the 

certified mean, or if two successive batch standards were greater than +/- 2 standard deviations 

on the same side of the mean.  A batch was also failed if a blank exceed 5 times the detection 

limit (50 PPB). This was modified to 10 times detection limit later in the program. In the event of 

a failed batch, reruns were requested on all or a portion of the batch submission.   

Assay results associated with failed insertions/batches are stored within the database but are 

not associated with sample interval information. 

Batch re-runs also include quality control samples. The database is updated with re-run data 

only when re-run batch passes all QA/QC requirements. Only final validated assay data is 

associated with sample intervals.  

A Table of Failures was maintained to document failures and resolutions. "Before and After" 

time series charts were maintained to monitor lab re-run analysis on the standards and blanks. 

Scatter charts were maintained for the three duplicate types. These charts facilitated validation 

and allowed identification of bias and/or drift within the primary and secondary labs used for 

gold analysis. 

15.2 Drill Database Construction and Verification 

15.2.1 B2Gold - Project La Libertad, 2010-2011 

All current drill hole data is initially captured onto paper formats. Data is subsequently entered 

into drill hole specific MS-Excel workbooks employing true dual data entry methods. A 

comparison/revision of the workbook pairs is completed and the data is subjected to a final 

verification with the original data capture forms. Logic checks within the Excel workbooks 

identify simple interval/depth errors. Validated data from the final Excel workbook was imported 

into the final database which is maintained in MS-Access. The database includes import tables 

containing collar and downhole surveys, detailed geological and geotechnical logs, specific 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 34  
   
 

gravity, and core box inventory data. Additional logic check queries within the database facilitate 

further data validation. 

Capture errors, encountered during data entry/initial validation, were corrected by the rig 

geologist on the original data form when possible and subsequently corrected within the Excel 

file. Errors encountered and corrected subsequent to publication of the database are tracked in 

a metadata table within the database. Edits are indicated on the original capture forms and 

annotated to the scans. 

The database paper files are in good order with all original paper capture forms filed by drill hole 

ID. All original paper capture forms are scanned and digitally archived. A complete archive of 

core photographs is maintained. Monthly reports which include summaries of QA/QC 

performance were prepared for B2Gold management. 

The current project database was constructed by Mike Glover, B2Gold's database manager for 

Nicaragua. The database is maintained onsite by a dedicated database manager, under the 

supervision of Mr. Glover, the Author has relied on Mr. Glover, an independent consultant for 

verification of the database. The Author has supervised the development of the quality control 

procedures and verification protocols employed by B2Gold and is satisfied they follow CIM best 

practice guidelines.

17.1 Planned Metallurgical Test Work in 2011 

B2Gold intends to look at gold and silver recovery characteristics on the Jabali vein system by

18.0 MINERAL RESOURCE ESTIMATE 

18.1 Data used for Grade Estimation 

Although a portion of the Jabali vein system had been previously explored and mined in the late 

1800's and early 1900's none of this data has been recovered with a sufficient degree of 

confidence for use in this resource estimation. 

In 2010, B2Gold completed surface trenching followed by a drill campaign on the Jabali vein 

structure consisting of 55 drill holes for a total of 9,659 metres. The average drill spacing along 

the mineralized structure was approximately 75 metres. The table below outlines a summary of 

drilling and trenching completed in 2010 and usage for the resource estimation exercise. 

Campaign Number of Holes Meters Type Usage 

2010 55 9659.4 DDH Used 

2009-2010 23 777 Trench-vein Used for Interpretation only 

2009-2010 8 305 Trench-colluvium Not Used -Did not intersect vein 

 

Surface trench data was used to guide the location and thickness of the interpretations. 

However, because of the quantity of fill material and concerns regarding the sampled material, 

such data could not be used for grade estimation. 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 36  
   
 

The database used for this resource estimate was compiled by Martha Sanchez and Mike 

Glover, the La Libertad database managers. Final assays for 2010 drilling were received on 

February 8th, 2011. 

All information used for this resource estimate was verified prior to use.  

18.2 Geological Domains 

Gold and silver mineralization at the Jabali vein system occurs within low sulphidation 

epithermal veins and stockwork systems hosted by andesitic volcanic rocks. High grade gold 

(~>1 g/t gold) occurs within brecciated quartz veins with banded, and vuggy textures. Moderate 

silica alteration occurs within the host rock in the hanging wall stockwork material. 

True vein widths vary from 1 to 17 metres with an average of approximately 5 metres. True 

stockwork widths vary from 3 to 30 metres with an average of approximately 14 metres. 

Stockwork widths are inclusive of veins. The Jabali vein has been subdivided into 3 main 

domain zones. From west to east they are: Antenna, Central, and Momotombo. These roughly 

coincide with the areas defined by previous mining in the 1800's. 

The Jabali vein has been subdivided into 3 main zones. From west to east they are: Antenna, 

Central, and Momotombo. These roughly coincide with the areas defined by previous mining. 

Three geologic mineralized units have been interpreted and modeled in three dimensions for the 

grade estimation exercise: Quartz stockwork (QZST), quartz breccias (QZBH), and galleries 

(GAL) (old mined workings). 

Quartz Stockwork (QZST) 

The quartz stockwork zone outlines are based on logged lithology and quartz vein percentage 

obtained from the primary logging forms. This zone forms an outer envelope of mineralized 

material and is inclusive of QZBH material. 

Quartz-Breccia (QZBH) 

QZBH outlines were originally interpreted strictly on logged lithology and quartz vein percent; 

however, these outlines included numerous low grade samples that contrasted significantly with 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 37  
   
 

high grade cores. Frequently very sharp contrasts exist between low and high grade material 

and this contrast would have been problematic during grade estimation. To improve grade 

differentiation, the QZBH outlines were modified to include only material that was markedly 

higher grade in gold than background, generally around 1 g/t  gold. A nominal minimum 

horizontal thickness of 2 metres was used however flexibility was permitted on this rule. 

Efforts have begun to further categorize the QZBH and QZST rock types based on accessory 

mineral occurrences and textures. Although this data wasn't available for this resource estimate, 

it is hoped this may better differentiate high and low grade gold assays on a geological basis. 

Galleries (GAL) 

The Jabali vein was mined from underground in the mid-20th century. Very little documentation 

of the extent of this mining exists today. The best remaining piece of information is an individual 

long section showing drifts and stopes at Jabali. Although inadequate to be used quantitatively, 

the historic long section gives an indication to the location and scale of previous mining at 

Jabali.  

Drill hole intervals logged as galleries (GAL) and fill (RELL) were grouped and linked hole to 

hole to form outlines of mined out material during modeling to account for the mined out areas. 

Occasionally, intervals with logged rock codes were tagged as gallery if continuity with 

surrounding mined out regions necessitated and the logged interval recorded very low 

recoveries (generally below 20%) during drilling. 

The above interpretations were completed on 50 to 100 metre spaced vertical, north-south 

cross sections. The sectional interpretations were reconciled on levels to produce a consistent 

3-dimensional interpretation. 

Colluvium, saprolite and saprock (CUBR, SADO, SAPR) 

For geotechnical reasons and to assign suitable densities, solid models were created for 

material logged as colluvium, saprolite and saprock. 

In each case, the vertical thickness of each material was calculated using logged intervals in 

drill holes and the current topographic surface. These thicknesses were interpolated to fill the 

entire Jabali area. A thickness surface was then subtracted from the topography surface to 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 38  
   
 

produce the final bottom of unit surface (i.e. (Current topo)-(saprolite thickness) = (bottom of 

saprolite)).  

The average saprolite thickness is 12 metres from surface and the average saprock thickness is 

19 metres below surface.  

Figure 18-1:  Antenna Zone- Surface Geology

Wireframing 

Three dimensional (3D) computer wireframes (or solids) of the QZBH, QZST and GAL zones 

were created by linking interpretations on vertical cross sections (see section 18.2 for 

  



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 40  
   
 

description). Sections were added where more detail was required. The wireframes were 

extended at least 100 metres from drilling along strike and down dip. 

Wireframes were validated in 3 ways to ensure they adequately represent the volumes of the 

modeled units: 

1. Visual comparison of wireframes to drill holes on sections and levels. When areas of 

concern were found, the interpretations were corrected and new wireframes were 

created. This process was completed several times until no visually obvious biases 

were observed. 

2. Software validation of wireframes to ensure they are closed and do not contain 

overlaps. 

3. Comparison of the calculated horizontal thickness of intercepts to wireframe 

horizontal thickness on long section. Any areas of concern were corrected. A long 

section showing the intercept versus model horizontal thickness is shown in 

Appendix 6. These long sections show only QZBH thickness and ignore the internal 

gallery content (i.e. it compares the QZBH wireframe to theoretical "pre-mining" 

intervals). The interpretation/wireframe thicknesses were adjusted accordingly.

18.4 Exploratory Data Analysis (EDA) 

Descriptive statistics and comparisons of logged lithologies and mineralization types were 

carried out to examine gold and silver distribution patterns. Despite the high quality of logging, 

only a few key (and intuitive) features correlate well with precious metal grades. (see 

Appendix 4). 

Gold and silver mineralization are most closely associated with logged lithology and quartz vein 

percentage and to lesser extent quartz type. 

The highest grade primary mineralization code captured during logging is quartz-breccia 

(QZBH) followed by quartz-stockwork (QZST) and quartz-vein (QZVN). Other brecciated host 

rock types and structures, andesite volcanic breccias (ANBV), andesite breccias (ANBX) and 

tectonic breccias (TCBH) contain anomalous values, however they are still quite low grade and 

represent minor components of the data set. 

The quantity of quartz veining is also an excellent predictor of mineralization; however, this is 

somewhat redundant since primary lithologies of QZST and QZBH by definition incorporate 

quartz vein quantities. Quartz vein percent has been grouped in the charts below for simplicity. 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 42  
   
 

B2Gold had anticipated that vein textures could help further distinguish between lower and 

higher grade gold distributions within the mineralized QZBH structure. Gold and silver grades 

correlate best with vuggy quartz and other textures (massive, drusy, banded) show a moderate 

positive correlation. Crystalline quartz has a negative indicator of grade. Although textures help 

in distinguishing high and low gold and silver grades, they cannot be used in isolation. 

Logged alteration intensity did not show any strong correlations with gold grades. There is weak 

to moderate positive correlation between silica alteration and gold, although vein percent is 

usually a better indicator. Argillic alteration shows a weak negative correlation to gold grades. 

Logged sphalerite occurrences exhibit has a strong correlation to higher gold grades, whereas 

logged galena shows a weaker correlation. All other sulphides and oxides have no obvious 

correlation. 

Accordingly, the best grades at the Jabali vein system are associated with quartz breccia veins 

with vuggy, drusy and banded quartz textures and observable sphalerite. 

Silver/gold ratio within the QZBH zone is approximately 14:1 for assays greater than 0.5 g/t 

gold, although with a correlation coefficient of 0.4 there is considerable variability in the 

relationship.  

Appendix 4 contains a more thorough compilation of EDA charts and statistics. 

The charts below show the average gold grade of these various features.

18.5 Compositing 

Two separate compositing methods were used for the Jabali inferred resource estimate.  

• Within the QZBH zone, intervals were calculated as "whole vein" composites 

broken at gallery intersections. This method was used because there was a 

problem in early estimates with wide (multi-composite) intersections overpowering 

narrow (single composite) intersections. The minimum QZBH composite length is 

0.7 metres and the maximum was 16.5 metres. The very narrow intervals generally 

occur adjacent to mined out areas, representing what was left by previous mining. 

• Within the stockwork zone (QZST) a nominal 3 metre composite length was used. 

Composite lengths within zones were permitted to vary a little to avoid residuals at 

the end of intervals. The 3 metre length was chosen based on the zone width, 

grade variability across the zone and likely mining method/SMU size. 

Final capped composite statistics for each domain are shown in the chart below. Only codes 

100 (QZBH) and 200 (QZST) were assigned grade in the mineral resource estimate (see 

Appendix 2). 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report

18.7 Block Model Parameters 

A 3D block model was created to cover enough area at the Jabali vein system to allow for pit 

optimization. Blocks were filled below topography and within the zone wireframes. Blocks were 

permitted to be sub-celled according to the limits presented in the table below.  

 X Y Z

Number 350 400 90 
Size 12 3 6

0.1 metre in 
zones 

0.1 metre (at topo) 
3 metres in zones 

 

Each block was assigned a domain code and specific gravity according to its material type. 

18.8 Estimation Plan 

"Hard" boundaries were used between stockwork (QZST) and quartz-breccia (QZBH) domains. 

Given that the grade differential at the contact of these two domains is frequently dramatic from 

0.5 to 0.8 g/t gold in QZST to 4 to 5 g/t gold in QZBH this approach was warranted. 

A three pass approach was used for grade estimation. Pass 1 and 2 required at least 2 drill 

holes for estimation, while pass 3 permitted estimation with just 1 drill hole (no material from 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 49  
   
 

Pass 3 was included in the inferred mineral resource tabulation). Details of the search ellipse 

size, orientation and composite selection criteria are given in the table below. 

 PASS 1 PASS 2 PASS 3 
Primary Direction (X) 90 135 180 
Secondary (Y) 25 37.5 50 
Tertiary (Z) 65 97.5 130 
Min (QZBH/QZST) 3/4 3/4 1/3 
Max (QZBH/QZST) 6/12 6/10 3/10 
Max per DH (QZBH/QZST) 2/3 2/3 2/3 

 

Search ellipses were oriented using Datamine's "Dynamic Anisotropy" method where the 

orientation of the ellipse is estimated at each block using the orientation of the wireframes of 

that domain. These values are stored in the block model and used to re-orient the ellipse at 

each block. Additionally, the variogram models were re-oriented by the same method for the 

ordinary kriged model (used for sensitivity only). 

On average, the ellipses primary axes rake 30 degrees to the west on an east-west plane 

dipping 15 degrees to the north. 

Gold and silver grades were estimated using inverse distance to the power of 3 (ID3). Nearest 

neighbour (NN) and ordinary kriged (OK) models were estimated for comparison. The ID3 

model was chosen over the Kriged model due to extremely poor variography. Poor variography 

should not be surprising given the variability of grades in this type of deposit, the paucity of drill 

holes (only 55 drilled along 3.5 kilometre strike length) and the fact there is no close spaced drill 

information available. 

18.9 Categorization 

Inferred blocks were selected using polygons on long section that were drawn based on the 

rules below. 

 

 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 50  
   
 

Inferred: 

 - Blocks estimated within 90 x 25 x 65 metre search ellipse using minimum of 2 drill 
holes AND at most 75 metres to nearest single drill hole 

OR 

 - Blocks estimated within 120 x 37.5 x 97.5 metre search ellipse using minimum of 2 
drill holes AND at most 50 metres to nearest single drill hole 

The polygon selection was used to create a logical contiguous shape. A very small number of 

blocks are included that do not meet the criteria below. Similarly, some blocks that meet the 

criteria are excluded but form isolated pockets of little significance. 

Near surface blocks at Central were included that do not meet the criteria on the basis that 

trenches in the area indicate the vein does continue to surface (geologic continuity). 

See Appendix 6 & 8 for a long section showing the inferred resource outline in a dark green 

solid line. 

18.10 Block Model Validation 

Three methods were used to validate the block model: 

1. visual inspection of cross sections and levels 

2. comparison of global average grades using various estimation methods 

3. comparison of average grades by easting and elevation (swath plots) 

Inspection of Cross-sections and levels 

A complete set of sections and levels can be found in Appendix 7. These show composite grade 

and lithology as well as final block model grades. 

The following observations are made: 



B2Gold Corp. 
Jabali Project, La Libertad Region, Nicaragua 
NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report 
 

   
12 May 2011  Page 51  
   
 

1. Overall, the grade estimation mimics composite grade very well, especially in 

inferred blocks. The degree of smoothing seems suitable. 

2. Some "bleeding" of grade occurs across hanging wall and footwall within the QZBH. 

Although this has minor impact and, could be argued that it's desired, a narrower 

ellipse dimension across the vein may be warranted to limit its effect. Additional 

drilling will address this. 

Long sections containing the aggregate grade in QZBH are presented in Appendix 8. 

Global statistics 

The tables below show composite and block model average grades at a 0 g/t gold cutoff. As 

shown below, the global means compare within 5 to 10%, which is reasonable for an inferred 

resource and indicates that any global bias present is minimal.

Easting and Elevation average Grade Plots ("Swath" Plots) 

The charts below show that the various models track Nearest Neighbour (NN) grades very well. 

The ordinary kriged model shows a high degree of smoothing with a possible over-projection of 

grade at peaks and valleys. The inverse distance cubed (ID3) model shows moderate 

smoothing compared to the NN model and the grades generally agree very well. Larger 

differences are present in very low tonnage areas, but are considered inconsequential for the 

level of this study.

Comparison to other methods 

The following tables show a comparison between grade and tonnage estimates using different 

interpolation methods. The comparison was only done on "QZBH" material since only QZBH 

resources were calculated using the polygonal method. Since >90% of the resource as Jabali is 

contained within the QZBH domain, this was considered a suitable exercise. 

The polygonal model was completed on inclined long section using the same composites as for 

block model interpolations. Polygonal resources are stated as follows: 

1. Antenna zone: 50 metre polygons 

2. Central: 50 metre + ½ (50 to 75 metre) polygons 

3. Momotombo: 50 metre polygons

NI 43-101 Resource Estimate Technical Report

Inclined long sections showing the polygons and the block model inferred outline are presented 

in Appendix 9. 

The various models behave as expected compared to one another, with the ordinary kriged 

(OK) model being the smoothest (with lower grade, but higher tonnage) and the polygonal 

model being the least smooth (lower tonnes, higher grade).  

Given the disparate methodology and categorization, these models compare quite well and lend 

support to the validity of the resource model.
